<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b083dfaf-a804-412d-bc17-ac1e905baa88'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

  <span id="freeText1595720292965027756" style="display:none">Rousing pulp action and steampunk come together in a heartbreaking story of high adventure and alternate history.<br /><br />In the year 1870, a horrible plague of vampires swept over the northern regions of the world. It is now 2020 and a bloody reckoning is coming. Princess Adele is heir to the Empire of Equatoria, a remnant of the old tropical British Empire. When she becomes the target of a merciless vampire clan, her only protector is the Greyfriar, a mysterious hero who fights the vampires from deep within their territory. Their dangerous relationship plays out against an approaching war to the death between humankind and the vampire clans.<br /><br />The first book in a trilogy of high adventure and alternate history. Combining rousing pulp action with steampunk style, the Vampire Empire series brings epic political themes to life within a story of heartbreaking romance, sacrifice, and heroism.</span>

<div id="review_101483427" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101483427" />
    <a title="Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3039709-michelle-the-bookshelf-stalker-queen-of-the-undead"><img alt="Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328667000p2/3039709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/101483427?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead" href="/user/show/3039709-michelle-the-bookshelf-stalker-queen-of-the-undead">Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101483427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15799727905238637155">Update- Book 2 is The Rift Walker (Vampire Empire, #2), it will come out in September 2011, Yeah!!!<br/><br/>Review is still below: :) <br/><br/><br/>The rambling review of a book fanatic…<br/><br/>I finished the book and I hugged it. Yup, I’m gonna admit it. I hugged the book. It was THAT good. You are going to have many reviews for this book that will do an awesome job of detailing what the book is about and they will do a much better job of explaining the story. Therefore, I am going to do a funky bullet point list of what I l</span>
  <span id="freeText15799727905238637155" style="display:none">Update- Book 2 is The Rift Walker (Vampire Empire, #2), it will come out in September 2011, Yeah!!!<br /><br />Review is still below: :) <br /><br /><br />The rambling review of a book fanatic…<br /><br />I finished the book and I hugged it. Yup, I’m gonna admit it. I hugged the book. It was THAT good. You are going to have many reviews for this book that will do an awesome job of detailing what the book is about and they will do a much better job of explaining the story. Therefore, I am going to do a funky bullet point list of what I loved about this book and what I did not like.<br />What I loved about this book:<br /><br />•	The characters- The book is full of them. These are not your superficial I’ll-put-you-in-to-take-up-pages characters but characters with meaning and a story behind each one. You have Princess Adele, the main character of the story. In addition to Adele, you have (and this is just a few of them) Greyfriar (but who is he really?), Clark- the American War Hero (again- who is he really?), Colonel Anhalt (I loved him- he is so sweet), Lord Kelvin (I think he will be big in book 2), Mamoru (such an interesting character), Selkirk, Simon and one of my favorite characters Flay. The characters are so well written, I was never confused. Trust me, that is saying plenty!<br /><br />•	The combining of genres- The book combines horror, romance, action, adventure, politics, war, steampunk, and satire with such ease that you don’t even realize you are reading a book outside your comfort zone because it blends so perfectly. <br /><br />•	The imagery- holy cow can the authors write (can you tell I cant!). The best I can do is give you an example-<br /><br />“Adele saw dark mounds scattered on the avenues, streets, and alleys. A closer examination revealed that the mounds were piles of dead bodies. The city’s wide circles and narrow courtyards were heaped with bones. The turgid river Thames was at low tide and, as the airship skimmed over it, Adele saw white femurs and rib cages protruding from the muck along the shoreline. Nearly all the glass windows in the city were smashed, except amazingly, some of the stained glass of….”<br /><br />•	The vampires- These vampires are not your typical vampires. It would be easy to say they are vile, horrific, simplistic creatures that either destroyed or imprisoned most of the humans in the “Great Killing” of 1870 but that would be far from the truth. I cannot really explain the vampires since one of the rewards of reading the story is learning about the vampires as Adele does. Not everything is what it seems.<br /><br />Ok, so I am going to stop now since as the top line states… I am rambling. I forgot to write about what I did not like about the book…. It ended.<br /><br />Definitely my favorite book of 2010. A 6 star out of 5 (yup, I just wrote 6 out of 5).</span>
  <a data-text-id="15799727905238637155" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_137374459" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137374459" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137374459?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of alternate history, steampunk and adventure based fantasy</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Stacia (the 2010 club) by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=alternate-history-or-future">alternate-history-or-future</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137374459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7410213595094268870"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Soon he would have to reveal himself to her, and he knew what her reaction would be. <br/>His numb heart broke at that realization.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>What to say, what to say, what to say...<br/><br/><b>Swashbuckling Adventure! Political Intrigue! Forbidden Desire!</b><br/><br/>My apologies in advance for the sheer amount of quotes I'm saddling you with this time. I tried to cut back as much as possible, but I was so in love with the imagery through words in <i>The Greyfriar</i> that I had such a hard time choosing what to include and what </span>
  <span id="freeText7410213595094268870" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Soon he would have to reveal himself to her, and he knew what her reaction would be. <br>His numb heart broke at that realization.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>What to say, what to say, what to say...<br><br><b>Swashbuckling Adventure! Political Intrigue! Forbidden Desire!</b><br><br>My apologies in advance for the sheer amount of quotes I'm saddling you with this time. I tried to cut back as much as possible, but I was so in love with the imagery through words in <i>The Greyfriar</i> that I had such a hard time choosing what to include and what to leave out. My absolute favorite quotes would have been spoilers so I had to sorrowfully (dramatic much?) leave those out. <br><br>I got so many warm fuzzies from this book and this isn't even a "warm fuzzy" kind of book. When blood is spurting everywhere and heads are-a-rolling, you'd think I would find no time to say things such as <i>awww</i>. But I did. And I think I said (or at least thought) it quite often. <br><br>You might ask - what kind of book is this exactly? Let's see if I can come up with an appropriate answer. The closest I could probably get to defining a genre would be something along the lines of Alternate History/Steampunk with aspects of horror, mystery, and traditional fantasy politicking. There is the potential for romance, but the connection between characters dances on a line of 'want what you can't have,' so my guess it that we'll have at least a book or two of heavy sexual tension before any deals are sealed on that front. The first half of this book read closer to a traditional fantasy. I was enthralled from the get-go (how can you go wrong with a kidnap scene thrown in almost right off the bat?), but a couple of my reading buddies took several chapters before they started to warm up to the story because of the heavy emphasis on wars, factions and racial politicking upfront. If you are the type to struggle with this sort of dry information dump, I'd ask you to consider giving the book at least a few chapters. There is something magical about the interaction between the Greyfriar and Adele which will suck you into the story.<br><br><b>Speaking of the Greyfriar and Adele...</b> Is there ever a time in the history of ever when a mysterious masked man isn't intriguing and sexy? EVER? How could you not want to know who this person is? It's like V for Vendetta or Zorro all over again - JUST LET US LOOK BEHIND THE MASK!<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I wear a mask to hide my true self."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Plus, the man knows his way around a rapier (that's a special skinny sword-thing, not a bad sexual act). Yes, that would equal double swoon points. <br><br><b>But then, there's Gareth, the unusual vampire prince holding the princess hostage...</b> He's taken a curious interest in Adele. What are his motives? Is he wanting to protect her or use her?<br><br>It's an interesting take on a vampiric world when you realize that the vampires are the ones holding most of the power. I was fascinated that they'd used brute force to make humans do all of their work, so that they had no use for knowledge of menial, everyday tasks. If the vampires needed something, they'd steal or force a human to make or get them what they needed. It was so extreme that their society had little use for even the written word or many necessities of human-kind.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"We use your clothes because your skin is too fragile to wear."<br><br>"Would it insult you if I used your alphabet? I don't think I could start from scratch."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Gareth and Adele's interactions were quite amusing. At times I felt like Adele was the teacher and Gareth was not much more than a child because his social graces were extremely lacking. I was almost vaguely reminded of Tarzan and Jane.<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Well, newborns could well nurse their mothers to death." Gareth waved a dismissive hand. "Things happen."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Don't worry about the meat. It is cow. And some horse. That is acceptable to humans, yes?"<br>"Horse? No! Civilized people don't eat horses. We ride them. Oh God, have you fed me horse?"</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Actually, horse can be considered a delicacy in many countries, which means that it might <i>be</i> viewed by some as food for civilized people. Not that I would know. I have yet to try horse and doubt I ever will.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380343156i/698725._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>I really wish there was a way to explain the way that I felt while reading <i>The Greyfriar</i>. Horse meat aside - it's almost as if I'd been snacking on books which weren't fully satisfying my hunger and then I stumbled upon one which satiated me.<br><br>The imagery was raw, gory and sometimes beautiful. You felt like you were dropped right there in the middle of a scene.<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>The palace's decrepit decorations were overwhelmed by piles of bone and hundreds of skulls staring down from broken chandeliers. Vampires slouched along the walls, drunk with blood, sometimes with red hands resting on humans who still showed signs of life.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>And did I say there were humorous moments too?<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"I'm sorry, but watching a vampire talk politics is like putting a gown on an ape and calling it a duchess."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>This book might not be for everyone, but I loved it.<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>His whole species was damned, but he didn't care.<br>He looked up, his breath a shuddering inhale. "I will always protect you."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Thanks Joan, Crystal, Rebecca and Amanda for the buddy read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7410213595094268870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_508767695" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/508767695" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/508767695?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">readers of the Parasol Protectorate</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer508767695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12169542417673053921"><br/>Would you like some wine with your pastiche?*<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6381205.Soulless__Parasol_Protectorate___1_' title='Soulless (Parasol Protectorate, #1) by Gail Carriger' rel='nofollow noopener'>Soulless</a> meets <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41428.Beauty' title='Beauty by Robin McKinley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Beauty</a>, shares meaningful whispers and lingering gazes, then elopes to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8909.The_War_of_the_Worlds' title='The War of the Worlds by H.G. Wells' rel='nofollow noopener'>The War of the Worlds</a>, undoubtedly to spawn a trilogy (if they sell well).<br/><br/>Understand, I didn't mean to read this. But it was a recent monthly read, and I'm trying to be more open minded about urban fantasy. Why? Because I desperately want to believe in the worlds urban fantasy creates--if they weren't so glaringly awful at it. <br/><br/>This is not awful.<br/><br/>This is, however, fair</span>
  <span id="freeText12169542417673053921" style="display:none"><br />Would you like some wine with your pastiche?*<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6381205.Soulless__Parasol_Protectorate___1_" title="Soulless (Parasol Protectorate, #1) by Gail Carriger" rel="nofollow noopener">Soulless</a> meets <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41428.Beauty" title="Beauty by Robin McKinley" rel="nofollow noopener">Beauty</a>, shares meaningful whispers and lingering gazes, then elopes to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8909.The_War_of_the_Worlds" title="The War of the Worlds by H.G. Wells" rel="nofollow noopener">The War of the Worlds</a>, undoubtedly to spawn a trilogy (if they sell well).<br /><br />Understand, I didn't mean to read this. But it was a recent monthly read, and I'm trying to be more open minded about urban fantasy. Why? Because I desperately want to believe in the worlds urban fantasy creates--if they weren't so glaringly awful at it. <br /><br />This is not awful.<br /><br />This is, however, fairly obvious.<br /><br />The most interesting twist in this world is that the vampires came out of the shadows in 1870, slaughtering millions and overtaking most of the cooler zones of the world. (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6690798.The_Passage__The_Passage___1_" title="The Passage (The Passage, #1) by Justin Cronin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Passage</a>). Humanity retreated to the tropics and has slowly regrouped, rebuilding nations along the old lines of the British Protectorates, the USA, China and other various world-powers.<br /><br />The humans are finally starting to feel ready to take the war back to the vampires, and a political alliance has been made with <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/ArrangedMarriage" rel="nofollow noopener">an arranged marriage </a> between a British princess and an American Senator. As he heads to the Empire to seal the deal, <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/PluckyGirl" rel="nofollow noopener"> the plucky Princess </a>is riding a heavily fortified dirigible to northern fringe nations on a goodwill mission, and her younger brother is along for the ride. Like many heroines, she is Destined for Greater Things, but she has No Clue About her Special Powers (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13995.Winds_of_Fate__Valdemar_Mage_Winds___1_" title="Winds of Fate (Valdemar Mage Winds, #1) by Mercedes Lackey" rel="nofollow noopener">Winds of Fate</a>). Vampires attack the dirigible, it crashes, and she quickly discovers she and her brother are the target of the attack. Shortly after, she meets the legendary Greyfriar, a semi-mythical <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/MysteriousPast" rel="nofollow noopener">mysterious figure</a> who fights for humanity in the north (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7108001.Abraham_Lincoln_Vampire_Hunter" title="Abraham Lincoln Vampire Hunter by Seth Grahame-Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">Abraham Lincoln: Vampire Hunter</a>). Greyfriar safely gets her to a village <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/ItsNotYouItsMyEnemies" rel="nofollow noopener">and leaves.</a><br /><br />MAJOR SPOILERS FOLLOW SO THAT I CAN MOCK THEM. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Heroine is captured and <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/GirlInTheTower" rel="nofollow noopener">imprisoned in a tower</a> so that the King of the London Vampires can interrogate her. The King intends to <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/TakeOverTheWorld" rel="nofollow noopener">take over the world.</a> Her capture gives her American fiance and her father a chance to rouse the populace to battle <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/DamselInDistress?from=Main.DistressedDamsel" rel="nofollow noopener">under pretext of rescue.</a> Meanwhile, we meet a <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/EnlightenmentSuperpowers" rel="nofollow noopener">clandestine group of special advisors</a> who attempt to mount their own rescue mission, if no other reason than to assure the fiance she is still alive and further hint at her Special But Unknown Powers. During her imprisonment, she gets to know the brooding <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/CainAndAbel" rel="nofollow noopener">brother of the Evil Vampire</a>, who has recently returned after <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/ByronicHero" rel="nofollow noopener">self imposed exile</a>. Eventually, Greyfriar appears to help her escape. She gets away, meets back up with <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/SecretIdentity" rel="nofollow noopener">Greyfriar</a> and he takes her off to his castle where she learns vampires are human too (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1603923.Beauty_and_the_Beast" title="Beauty and the Beast by Walt Disney Company" rel="nofollow noopener">Beauty and the Beast</a>). There is a side plot where King Vamp's Captain of the Guard has a <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/IfICantHaveYou" rel="nofollow noopener">strange fascination</a> for Gareth, the brooding brother. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I enjoyed the idea of vampires used in an apocalypse type scenario, and then smashing it into a steampunk novel. The lead heroine is specifically described as of a darker skin tone, taking after her Indian mother's side of the family. That's about the only multi-culti nod, but it could be a hint of more interesting development to come. As it is, it provides the <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/IAmNotPretty" rel="nofollow noopener"> reason she believes herself unattractive,</a> and a potential for alienation from the court.<br /><br />Otherwise, it was overly-burdened with unoriginal ideas. Although the reader is given a fair amount of background on the species difference of vampires, I still can't quite wrap my head around the visuals when the scenes focus on vampire-controlled cities.<br /><br />Writing was acceptable, even above average in the UF field. I don't mean to damn it with faint praise; that's a compliment from me. While it didn't soar, neither did it annoy with redundant word choice or simplistic structure. The story is decently paced with action scenes described well. I suspect it will appeal to fans of the Parasol Protectorate. While romance is an important part of the story, it is developed slowly, which may appeal to some readers.<br /><br />Three redundant stars.<br /><br />*For reference, similar books and tropes have been provided in links.<br /><br />Cross posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/03/15/the-greyfriar-by-clay-and-susan-griffith-or-i-know-ive-read-this-before/">http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/0...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12169542417673053921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_132265287" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132265287" />
    <a title="Jess the Romanceaholic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2807469-jess-the-romanceaholic"><img alt="Jess the Romanceaholic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1298615023p2/2807469.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132265287?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess the Romanceaholic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess the Romanceaholic" href="/user/show/2807469-jess-the-romanceaholic">Jess the Romanceaholic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Steampunk and Adventure novels</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jess the Romanceaholic by: </span>
      Just about EVERYONE
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2807469-jess-the-romanceaholic?shelf=2010-read">2010-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2807469-jess-the-romanceaholic?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2807469-jess-the-romanceaholic?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2807469-jess-the-romanceaholic?shelf=auto-buy">auto-buy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2807469-jess-the-romanceaholic?shelf=tortured-hero">tortured-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2807469-jess-the-romanceaholic?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2807469-jess-the-romanceaholic?shelf=on-the-run">on-the-run</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2807469-jess-the-romanceaholic?shelf=secret-identity">secret-identity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2807469-jess-the-romanceaholic?shelf=apocalypse-now">apocalypse-now</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2807469-jess-the-romanceaholic?shelf=family-issues">family-issues</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132265287" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7357437817863529745">I swear I have no words, but dangit I'm going to try!<br/><br/>This book has a little bit of everything. There's steampunk, romance (the heartfelt kind, not the steamy kind), swashbuckling adventure, horror (complete with gore), politics, religion, family issues, intrigue, betrayal, all wrapped up int a giant ball of awesomeness. <br/><br/>What worked for me:<br/><br/>*The whole secret identity of Greyfriar. I actually had a hard time deciding who I liked better -- "Greyfriar" or his alter-ego, <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Prince Gareth <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(</a></span></span>
  <span id="freeText7357437817863529745" style="display:none">I swear I have no words, but dangit I'm going to try!<br /><br />This book has a little bit of everything. There's steampunk, romance (the heartfelt kind, not the steamy kind), swashbuckling adventure, horror (complete with gore), politics, religion, family issues, intrigue, betrayal, all wrapped up int a giant ball of awesomeness. <br /><br />What worked for me:<br /><br />*The whole secret identity of Greyfriar. I actually had a hard time deciding who I liked better -- "Greyfriar" or his alter-ego, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Prince Gareth <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />*The "sex talk" had me rolling, yet oddly disappointed that it wasn't discussed further :P I'm truly dying to learn more about the physiology and culture of the vampires. Which brings me to<br /><br />*The vampires. I. LOVED. how they managed to put a new spin on the "same old same old" vampire stories. Some of our commonly accepted vampire lore is fact (such as vampires being able to fly), some is only based on fact (such as the idea of vampires being unable to tolerate sunlight -- this is true, only not because they turn to ash; rather because they simply function better in colder temperatures), and some is purely fiction (such as vampires not having a reflection in a mirror). It kept things fresh while still appealing to fans of the "original" vampire mythologies.<br /><br />*The romance -- for once, I loved the fact that the "romance" wasn't in the forefront of the whole story. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8140709.The_Greyfriar__Vampire_Empire___1_" title="The Greyfriar (Vampire Empire, #1) by Clay Griffith" rel="nofollow noopener">The Greyfriar</a> is NOT about the blossoming affection between the hero and heroine, but rather is about this incredible world perched on the cusp of a terrible war, the nasty politics and prejudices boiling behind the scenes, and a small resistance desperately trying to set things straight. And yet, even with all of that, the romance felt REAL -- it was a slow build of affection, set back by betrayal and mistrust, but ultimately culminating in a love (rather than lust and chemistry) that I as a reader could actually <i>feel</i>.<br /><br />*I love the cats. :D<br /><br />*I really enjoyed watching Adele mature throughout the story, as her prejudices and preconceptions were constantly both reaffirmed and destroyed.<br /><br />*I admit, I like Flay, despite the fact she's one of The Bad Guys. <br /><br />*The "Steampunk" elements felt natural rather than being forced or simply used as window dressing to ride the wave of popularity that the genre is currently enjoying. It wasn't the "Victorian England only with automata and aviator goggles" feel that a lot of steampunk has -- this is a war-ravaged people with a whole different set of technology. Yes, there's steam engines, and yes there are airships (and even goggles lol) but there's also a strong emphasis on chemical weapons rather than clockwork. It's a VERY refreshing twist to the genre.<br /><br />*I also liked that even though this is OBVIOUSLY the setup for a series, it didn't feel bogged down with all the extra baggage that typically comes with pilot novels, AND more importantly, it ended at a satisfactory place. Yes, I will preorder the next novel just as soon as it becomes available to do so. However, I'm not left screaming my dismay at even a partial cliff-hanger ending, which is nice. <br /><br /><br />What didn't work for me:<br /><br />*The fact that the rest of the series isn't out yet! GAH! <br /><br />*The writing got a little odd at times.. Not "bad", just.. odd.. It was in third person, so it would refer to Adele by her name (as in, "Adele walked to the window."), but then it would turn around and refer to her as "the princess" or "the young woman" or whatever, which got a bit confusing at times.<br /><br />*The price. $10 on kindle is outside of my normal purchase range -- as a matter of principal I tend to stick to my $6.99 price points unless it's an author that I've read and enjoyed previously. All I can say is THANK HEAVENS FOR AMAZON GIFT CARDS because that's the only reason I bit the bullet on this one and trust me, this is one purchase I can honestly say is worth the extra.<br /><br />Overall? This one gets the honor of going on my Yes It's Really THAT Good shelf -- I would give this one WAY more than 5 Stars if it was possible.<br /><br />lol How's THAT for "having no words"?? :P</span>
  <a data-text-id="7357437817863529745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_692496337" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/692496337" />
    <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc"><img alt="Mogsy (MMOGC)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286325553p2/4379514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/692496337?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mogsy (MMOGC)" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc">Mogsy (MMOGC)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=war">war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=alternate-history">alternate-history</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer692496337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17446075109683865915">Note: I received a review copy of this book compliments of the publisher, in exchange for my honest opinions. Thanks, Pyr/Prometheus Books!<br/><br/>Vampires and steampunk! The former, obviously, is a topic that's been wildly popular for years and years. The latter, as well, has been a subgenre gaining more traction in the science fiction and fantasy world lately, hence the fact that I would finally stumble across a book which unites both concepts in the foundation for its story was only a matter of time!</span>
  <span id="freeText17446075109683865915" style="display:none">Note: I received a review copy of this book compliments of the publisher, in exchange for my honest opinions. Thanks, Pyr/Prometheus Books!<br /><br />Vampires and steampunk! The former, obviously, is a topic that's been wildly popular for years and years. The latter, as well, has been a subgenre gaining more traction in the science fiction and fantasy world lately, hence the fact that I would finally stumble across a book which unites both concepts in the foundation for its story was only a matter of time! What did strike me as a pleasant surprise, however, was finding a book that does this so well. <br /><br />The Greyfriar is set in an alternate history in which humans and vampires have been locked in a bitter war for more than a century. In 1870, the blood drinkers rose up to conquer the northern lands, driving the humans towards warmer climes. Now, the young princess Adele of Equatoria is to wed the famed vampire hunter senator of the American Republic, their marriage to be the start of an alliance to take back their lands. But a month before the wedding, an ambush on the princess' airship throws all plans into turmoil. Adele's way home now involves a partnership with the Greyfriar, a semi-legendary figure who has become a symbol of humanity's fight against the vampires.<br /><br />Notice I say "partnership with" and not "dependency upon", because as princesses go, Adele is far from your dainty damsel in distress and can most certainly hold her own. In this book, both the main protagonist and also the enemy vampire warchief are female characters one would not be wise to cross, as each woman has a commanding presence about them in their own way. With Adele, I loved her for her independence, intelligence, fighting skills, as well as for her protectiveness and love for her little brother. All the characters here are pretty well written, but it's extra nice having a heroine I genuinely like and enjoy reading about.<br /><br />Still, while I'm steadfastly rooting for Adele, it's hard not to be drawn to the vampires as well, with their fascinating empire, politics, family conspiracies and infighting among their peerage. The vampires in this book are atypical enough not to bore me, with their strange biological quirks allowing their bodies to be lighter and to "float" in the air, and it amuses me to no end how disdainful they are of human myths like the ones claiming vampires to be their own dead risen to life. Their culture is well defined, like everything else in this book's world.<br /><br />My favorite part, though, is the thread of romance woven through the second half of the book! Admittedly, as much as I enjoy love stories, romance in these types of books usually make me balk -- like, seriously, why spoil a perfectly awesome action adventure tale by forcing a contrived and cringe-worthy romantic side plot just for the sake of having it? And yet, the thing is, the love story in this book could not have been more natural and just...totally appropriate, like it belongs. I don't know what it is, but perhaps the fact that the authors are a married couple who have been writing and publishing together for years has something to do with it, because the attraction between Adele and Greyfriar felt passionate, gradual, sweet, real and -- most importantly -- earned. None of that insta-love nonsense.<br /><br />Plus, no worries if romance isn't your thing; as I've said, it's not the dominant focus and does not overtake the entire story, and I liked how there were just as many if not more action-oriented battles and fight scenes in this book. In fact, my only wish is that the novel was better paced and balanced. After a very bombastic introduction, it wasn't until halfway through the book that my enthusiasm spiked again, but once it did, you can be sure I was completely enamored. I read the second half all in one sitting, and loved every minute of it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17446075109683865915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137631971?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isamlq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isamlq" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer137631971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5634756010766714632">Here’s what the blurb on the back says, <br/><br/><i>“In the year 1870, a horrible plague of vampires swept over the northern regions of the world. Millions of humans were killed outright. Millions more died of disease and famine due to the havoc that followed. Within two years, once-great cities were shrouded by the grey empire of the vampire clans. Human refugees fled south to the tropics because vampires could not tolerate the constant heat there. They brought technology and a feverish drive to reestablis</i></span>
  <span id="freeText5634756010766714632" style="display:none">Here’s what the blurb on the back says, <br /><br /><i>“In the year 1870, a horrible plague of vampires swept over the northern regions of the world. Millions of humans were killed outright. Millions more died of disease and famine due to the havoc that followed. Within two years, once-great cities were shrouded by the grey empire of the vampire clans. Human refugees fled south to the tropics because vampires could not tolerate the constant heat there. They brought technology and a feverish drive to reestablish their shattered societies of steam and iron amid the mosques of Alexandria, the torrid quietude of Panama, or the green temples of Malaya. <br /><br />It is now 2020 and a bloody reckoning is coming. <br /><br />Princess Adele is heir to the Empire Equatoria, a remnant of the old tropical British Empire. She is quick with her wit as well as with a sword or gun. She is eager for an adventure before she settles into a life of duty and political marriage to a man she does not know. But her quest turns black when she becomes the target of a merciless vampire clan. Her only protector is the Greyfriar, a mysterious hero who fights the vampires from deep within their territory. Their dangerous relationship plays out against an approaching war to the death between humankind and the vampire clans.” </i><br /><br />The blurb did little to prepare me for the ride that I was about to take. OK. Hype, hype, hype. I know, but I think the book deserves all the hype it got when it was released. Here's why I think vampire lovers/ steampunk lovers/ YA lovers should read it (NOW):<br /><br /><b>Three words:</b> <i>Alternate. World. History.</i> <br /><b>Not enough?</b> How about <i>vampires…</i> and not the sparkly kind either. They’re merciless and they’re in control. Enter Adele and the mysterious Greyfriar. It is impossible, impossible, I tell you, not to fall in love with the lot of them. The writing is superb so much so you just want to root for them, because you totally understand what they want and where they’re coming from. <br /><br />So, merciless vampires meant action was a given… but the hints of romance were <b>freaking KICK ASS! <br /><br />READ IT! READ IT NOW! </b><br /></span>

<div id="review_1261484946" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1261484946" />
    <a title="Gergana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312798-gergana"><img alt="Gergana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439319393p2/5312798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1261484946?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gergana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gergana" href="/user/show/5312798-gergana">Gergana</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312798-gergana?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1261484946" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1783967219059813616">WOW! Starting from the gorgeous cover, the setting, the characters, the fights - this book is absolutely amazing! I honestly don't know how to write a review of <i>The Greyfriar</i> without spending hours praising its originality, world-building, character development and so on. <br/><br/>Imagine people on steam-powered ships fighting vampires in the air with some extra-cool gadgets that only human imagination can conceive. Or Vampires who can decrease their bodies' density so they can float on air and who have </span>
  <span id="freeText1783967219059813616" style="display:none">WOW! Starting from the gorgeous cover, the setting, the characters, the fights - this book is absolutely amazing! I honestly don't know how to write a review of <i>The Greyfriar</i> without spending hours praising its originality, world-building, character development and so on. <br /><br />Imagine people on steam-powered ships fighting vampires in the air with some extra-cool gadgets that only human imagination can conceive. Or Vampires who can decrease their bodies' density so they can float on air and who have driven the Europeans out of their lands and made London into their main stronghold where humans are kept as cattle or used as servants since vampires are no good at~ GAH! I can't even write a cohesive sentence without sounding like a total fangirl. Oh! And let's not forget the flashy bearded Americans with the white cowboy hats, the "British" (here, known as Equatorians) and their obsession with etiquette, the world-wide politics, the kick-ass heroine who has her weaknesses and fears, but is brave and strong-minded nevertheless, the Vampire princes, did I mention the awesome plot twists in the beginning? <br /><br />Dammit, ok, so, obviously, I liked it. But then, <b> why am I not giving it a 5-stars rating? </b> As much as I loved the whole idea of the book, there were a few major problems for me. <br /><br />1. Sometimes it felt like I was reading two completely different books - one of them is this epic adventure of two future rulers trying to prevent war, while the second one was a very slow, kind of cute, romance that was just too...Ok, I liked it, but it felt like it was trying to keep me away from the better, more action-packed parts of the book. I couldn't wait for the - I hate/like/hate/love/hate/not sure/like/etc. you part to be over so I can get to the fun.<br /><br />2. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ What the HELL is Greyfriar/Gareth doing? Why is he putting the lives of so many of his subjects at risk for one princess without even knowing her yet? Not once, not twice, but three times he takes the princess to some human friends, only for them to be massacred because of her presence afterwards! (True, this didn't happen in Edinburgh, but it could've!) I found his actions to be appalling and stupid and it took away from my enjoyment of the character.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />3. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Why are there no vampires in Edinburgh? What happened to them, why has noone found out about Prince Gareth's affection for humans? Has noone passed by the city and seen the freedom the humans there are enjoying? Don't know why, but this plot "convenience" bugged me. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />As a conclusion:<br />- This book is amazing! <br />- Audiobook is equally amazing! The narrator is absolutely brilliant, he even screams when he's supposed to (and managed to startle me a few times). He really puts a lot of skills and emotion in his performance and I would definitely recommend checking the Audiobook version!<br />- Will I read the sequels - yes, but not right away. Although I enjoyed it, I still feel there was something missing for me.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1783967219059813616" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

Hello? Five stars should speak for itself. Authors have a tendancy to write cha</span>
  <span id="freeText3459547008363787302" style="display:none">Love a book with a good strong name. The greyfriar, rolls off your tongue nicely doesn't it.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364143i/715725.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364143i/715726.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>This is gonna be a short review. Hello? Five stars should speak for itself. I want to highlight a few key things that blew me away.<br><br><br><br><b>1:</b> Not only is this a fantastical tale to work them poor missused brain muscles, but it is truly great literature. Not overly so. Will not bore you to tears. I promise.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364143i/715727.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><b>2:</b> I don't know about you, but I hate characters with no follow through. Authors have a tendancy to write characters that end up tooting their own horn or are all talk. <br><br>Love Gareth aka the Greyfriar. Not always hard for me to fall in love with the male lead character when I'm reading a book. The hard sell is always the female lead. They are never as strong as the writer portrays and they make stupid decisions. <br><br>Adele broke the habit. While the average tough female is saying, "I'm gonna mess you up". Adele walks past said female and proceeds to kick the ass of any baddie that stands in her way. She can also be very diplomatic when needed.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364143i/715728._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364143i/715729.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br><br><b>3:</b> Clay Griffith &amp; Susan Griffith wrote this series together. I am very fond of husband &amp; wife writing teams. It blows me away what can come of two great minds coming together. I don't think this would have been half as fantastic as it is had it been writer singularly.<br><br><br><br>I can see a Mrs. Greyfriar in the future. <i>Monsterzzz beware.</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364143i/715730.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364143i/715731.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="3459547008363787302" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_138181190" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/138181190" />
    <a title="Ahimsa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68163-ahimsa"><img alt="Ahimsa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425875981p2/68163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/138181190?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahimsa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahimsa" href="/user/show/68163-ahimsa">Ahimsa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138181190" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15054691114359700931">This is a book with a lot of buzz and good reviews, and the novel has some nice things going for it. The pace is frenetic; the action starts in the first chapter and rarely tapers off. The setting is creative and it's fun to think about the world the Griffiths have created. Basing humanity in the tropics was a stroke of world-building genius. But there are significant problems with the setting, plot, and characters.<br/>Character: The characters are really one-dimensional. Adele is yet another form o</span>
  <span id="freeText15054691114359700931" style="display:none">This is a book with a lot of buzz and good reviews, and the novel has some nice things going for it. The pace is frenetic; the action starts in the first chapter and rarely tapers off. The setting is creative and it's fun to think about the world the Griffiths have created. Basing humanity in the tropics was a stroke of world-building genius. But there are significant problems with the setting, plot, and characters.<br />Character: The characters are really one-dimensional. Adele is yet another form of Mary-Sue, destined for greatness and possessing unexplained unique skills. The development of her feelings toward Greyfriar was clumsily handled. The Senator is a cartoon character, as are most of the vampires. Anhalt is almost interesting, but we know too little of his story. He'd be an interesting link to the repercussions of vampires in Nepal--the mountains must be full of them but the Terrai would presumably be hot enough for them to avoid.<br />Setting: According to their bio, the authors were married in Scotland, but it didn't feel they knew it well. The Edinburgh castle is on a large hill, which isn't mentioned. Was there a remnant of the royal mile? Could you see Arthur's Seat? Or the Firth? There are none of the details that make a setting feel real here.<br />Plot: The plot was basic and seemed like an adventure from Rifts, complete with ley-line walkers. The foreshadowing was overdone on certain plot twists and they were overly obvious long before the reveal. The fast pace helped make up for these deficiencies, but it doesn't excuse it.<br />Particularly in a post-Twilight world, a book with vampires that respect humanity has to recreate the legend a bit. And indeed most of the traditional vampire mythos was debunked. Vampires can cast reflections, but cannot turn into wolfs or bats. This makes it all the stranger that crosses and churches still had power over the undead. (Who aren't really undead in this rendering).<br />All in all, this is light enough to feel like a comic book or video game. It's entertaining enough to read, but I'm not compelled to ever read more of the series. The steampunk elements are lightly applied, and the vampire story isn’t very new or interesting.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15054691114359700931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_137659714" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137659714" />
    <a title="oliviasbooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks"><img alt="oliviasbooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257619306p2/2843533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137659714?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="oliviasbooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="oliviasbooks" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks">oliviasbooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">lovers of steampunk and alternative history who do not mind a little zombie action</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to oliviasbooks by: </span>
      Kim + Michelle
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=i-cannot-tell-you-my-secret">i-cannot-tell-you-my-secret</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=love-story-romance">love-story-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=swapped-or-given-away">swapped-or-given-away</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=urban-fantasy-paranormal">urban-fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137659714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3546157715637194338">What a potent mixture: <br/>- An alternative history setting that has the human states and kingdoms huddled around the equator since the repelled-by-warmth vampire (<i>homo nosferatii</i>) clans crawled out of their hidden spots to initiate the Great Killing in 1870, leaving only enough human prey alive to keep as cattle herds.<br/>- Steampunk elements like pneumatic sailboats cruising the skies that somehow underline both the excotic atmosphere of the strange British-Egyptian-Persian Empire and the war-and-powe</span>
  <span id="freeText3546157715637194338" style="display:none">What a potent mixture: <br />- An alternative history setting that has the human states and kingdoms huddled around the equator since the repelled-by-warmth vampire (<i>homo nosferatii</i>) clans crawled out of their hidden spots to initiate the Great Killing in 1870, leaving only enough human prey alive to keep as cattle herds.<br />- Steampunk elements like pneumatic sailboats cruising the skies that somehow underline both the excotic atmosphere of the strange British-Egyptian-Persian Empire and the war-and-power-crazy American States, who have dropped a little farther south on the globe (Who doesn't hate Senator Clark with all her heart? do I ask).<br />- Gruesome horror scenes provided by cold-blooded, underestimated, zombie-like vampire clans who can fly by changing their bodies' density and who swoop down onto their human cattle leaving the streets of former Europe littered with mountains of decaying flesh and carpets of crunched bones.<br />- Action, action, action: A fearless, faceless vampire hunter, a brave princess skilled in martial arts, armies, vampires ambushes, traitors ...<br />- Dangerous politics, weak kings, cunning planners, advisers who are to be trusted or not to be trusted, a vampires prince with a craving to be human and a vampire prince with a craving to rule the world.<br />- Predudices, conceit, sibling love, hope, the essence of being human.<br />- Subtly changing points of view.<br />- A but later started sweet, sparkling and heart-warming Beauty-and-the-Beast-worthy impossible romance between a dashing, idealistic, vulnerable hero with an aching heart and a strong-willed and lovely heroine, which even includes a library (of fifteen volumes). <br />- An ending of the sort which ties most of the lose strands but wets your mouth for more adventures to come.<br /><br />What did I think? I thoroughly enjoyed it and I thought "What a potent mixture!" Didn't I say that already? <br />Recommended!<br /><br />Note: Although the date on the cover says "It's now 2010" this is no science fiction story set in the future. Apart from the steampunk elements the alternative history novel could be set still in the Victorian Era.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15863040164084842541">I am not sure why I enjoy some authors that write the steampunk genre and others I do not, but I found <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8140709.The_Greyfriar__Vampire_Empire___1_' title='The Greyfriar (Vampire Empire, #1) by Clay Griffith' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Greyfriar</a> was an interesting blend of family, an alternate reality and an unusual friendship. As in most first stories in a series, there was a heavy amount of time spent on introducing characters and building the storyline. I ran into some slow reading towards the beginning but once it took off, I was reading at a fast clip. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8140709.The_Greyfriar__Vampire_Empire___1_' title='The Greyfriar (Vampire Empire, #1) by Clay Griffith' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Greyfriar</a> was <b>NOT</b> a light story. The vampires were portrayed </span>
  <span id="freeText15863040164084842541" style="display:none">I am not sure why I enjoy some authors that write the steampunk genre and others I do not, but I found <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8140709.The_Greyfriar__Vampire_Empire___1_" title="The Greyfriar (Vampire Empire, #1) by Clay Griffith" rel="nofollow noopener">The Greyfriar</a> was an interesting blend of family, an alternate reality and an unusual friendship. As in most first stories in a series, there was a heavy amount of time spent on introducing characters and building the storyline. I ran into some slow reading towards the beginning but once it took off, I was reading at a fast clip. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8140709.The_Greyfriar__Vampire_Empire___1_" title="The Greyfriar (Vampire Empire, #1) by Clay Griffith" rel="nofollow noopener">The Greyfriar</a> was <b>NOT</b> a light story. The vampires were portrayed as animalistic killers. Humans were simply food. <br /><br />I want to write this review without any spoilers. I enjoyed the Victorian vibe even though the year was 2020! Note: the story was published in 2010. I liked the odd friendship between Princess Adele and the Greyfriar and watching it evolve. After finishing the book, I immediately started <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10790180.The_Rift_Walker__Vampire_Empire___2_" title="The Rift Walker (Vampire Empire, #2) by Clay Griffith" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rift Walker</a>.</span>

<div id="review_320789999" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/320789999" />
    <a title="Alkyoni" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3720870-alkyoni"><img alt="Alkyoni" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275136874p2/3720870.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/320789999?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alkyoni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alkyoni" href="/user/show/3720870-alkyoni">Alkyoni</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Alkyoni by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer">Anzu The Great Destroyer</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3720870-alkyoni?shelf=series-in-progress">series-in-progress</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3720870-alkyoni?shelf=from-dusk-till-dawn">from-dusk-till-dawn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3720870-alkyoni?shelf=first-in-a-series">first-in-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3720870-alkyoni?shelf=say-anything">say-anything</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3720870-alkyoni?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3720870-alkyoni?shelf=the-anzu-files">the-anzu-files</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer320789999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13294330296095540545"><br/>The airship that is carrying princess Adele, heir to the throne of the Equatorian Empire, is under attack. Colonel Anhalt is desperately trying to protect her but soon their ship crashes into the hostile vampire grounds and the young girl is separated from him. Thankfully Adele is not alone. A man who is considered to be a legend among her people comes to her rescue and so their journey together begins.<br/><br/>I must admit that the first chapters of the book were hard for me to follow. English is not my</span>
  <span id="freeText13294330296095540545" style="display:none"><br />The airship that is carrying princess Adele, heir to the throne of the Equatorian Empire, is under attack. Colonel Anhalt is desperately trying to protect her but soon their ship crashes into the hostile vampire grounds and the young girl is separated from him. Thankfully Adele is not alone. A man who is considered to be a legend among her people comes to her rescue and so their journey together begins.<br /><br />I must admit that the first chapters of the book were hard for me to follow. English is not my mother tongue so the descriptions of the airship, the clothes and the landscapes in a steampunk manner had me googling every second page. <br /><br />Another thing that didn’t help in the early chapters was the frequent POV change between the characters. I wasn’t eager to leave the character in action only to follow another one that was concerned about court formalities.<br /><br />However, it didn’t take long for everything to fall into place and for me to leave all my whining behind. I came to appreciate the vivid descriptions as well as the pages that the authors dedicated to the better understanding of each character.<br /><br />I can't say much about Greyfriar, partly because I don't want to give away the plot and partly because my friend Anzu has claimed him as her own and I can't bring myself to stand in her way. I'll just say that he is one of the most beautifully portrayed characters that I've ever read about.<br /><br />So is Princess Adele. She never forgets who she is or her responsibility towards her people, but at the same time she is kind, gentle and capable of putting a good fight of her own when needed.<br /><br />There were parts in the story that these two reminded me of Beuaty and the Beast. That might be a little misleading, since Vampire Empire is not a romance, it's more like an adventure, but there is a hint in it and they do share some very sweet moments together.<br /><br />I also loved Colonel Anhald, the dedicated officer who failed to protect his princess. I wanted to give him a hug and tell him that it will be ok, but from what I understand his kind of soldier is not the hugging type. Oh, well...<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13294330296095540545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8747323054964257589"><br/>I really enjoyed this story!<br/><br/>This is the first book in the 'Greyfriar' Trilogy. <br/><br/>The story takes place 150 years after 'The Killing'. A time when the Vampires have come out of hiding, and take over the world. Humans have either escaped to other organized human settlements (in the south), or became 'blood slaves' to the Vampires (in the north). <br/><br/>The Vampires in 'this world' are viscous & merciless, and think nothing of the humans except as a source of food. <br/><br/>The characters and world building in this </span>
  <span id="freeText8747323054964257589" style="display:none"><br>I really enjoyed this story!<br><br>This is the first book in the 'Greyfriar' Trilogy. <br><br>The story takes place 150 years after 'The Killing'. A time when the Vampires have come out of hiding, and take over the world. Humans have either escaped to other organized human settlements (in the south), or became 'blood slaves' to the Vampires (in the north). <br><br>The Vampires in 'this world' are viscous &amp; merciless, and think nothing of the humans except as a source of food. <br><br>The characters and world building in this story are AMAZING!<br><br>Adele and Gareth relationship goes through many phases, which ultimately leads to one of absolute trust.<br>I LOVED that they were mortal enemies, and that they have responsibilities, and duties... and yet they still found love. *sigh*<br><br><a href="http://s1095.photobucket.com/albums/i477/hebbies37/review%20pics/?action=view&amp;current=nobodyelsematters.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380365434ra/717500.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I was quite impressed with this story, and look forward to reading what's going to happen next to Adele, Gareth, Caesar, and Senator Clark.<br><br></span>
